14:14 - i am a boy scout and the buddy system is one of the most crucial things we teach. A few summers ago, around 2020/2021, my mom and I noticed these 3 distinct knocks. We live on a farm in the woods, and no matter where we were, we could hear these knocks and they always came in 3s and always sounded the exact same distance away. My mom heard it from my grandpa's house, we could hear it from our house, once I was out back hosing something off out back and I could hear it coming from the woods. It got worse when me and 2 of my friends went down to the creek together to go swimming. I know these woods like the back of my hand, my mom and I walk down to the creek every summer. The whole walk down we didnt hear a single knock. but once we made it to the creek (which is a couple miles from my house), the knocking picked back up. my friends could hear it too, but this time it actually sounded like it was getting closer with each knock. we eventually got scared and packed up our stuff and started to walk back to my house. the whole time the knocking would follow us. the next day my friends and I were all sick, and we were bed ridden for almost a week. I had the worst nightmares that week. Ever since then we haven't heard a single knock, not even an explanation to the knocking. nobody else in the area heard it either, and you can hear everything that goes on in this area. When he mentioned the knocking in the tree lines, my heart dropped. We've had some pretty weird things happen here, but that was by far the weirdest.

If they weren't sure what shoes he was wearing, how could they be sure that the shoe print matched? Without the concrete knowledge of what shoes he was wearing, it's entirely possible (and just as likely) that it was just some kid in the woods' prints. A lot of things about this case are easily explained by parents not being reliable sources and the search being handled poorly. Guilt can fuck up your memories, so that '5 minutes' they weren't looking for him could have easily been 30 and they just didn't want to believe they had left him alone for that long.  Another theory I have is that he was still in the area when they went looking for him but didn't respond when they called his name -- imagine you're six years old, hiding in a bush to scare your parents, and your dad thinks you're missing. Perfect opportunity! It's much easier to scare someone when they actively think you're not there. But then you wait too long and suddenly everyone's panicked, and you start to worry that you're in trouble. Kids get scared easily, and (especially if there were harsh punishments in his house) are very motivated by the fear of getting in trouble. Maybe he actively didn't respond to the people calling his name because he was nervous they'd be mad at him, so he wandered into the woods to hide. The thick foliage was disorienting and by the time he was ready to go back, he couldn't find the campsite.

A lot of the "mystery" of this case seems to depend on the assumption that the "dad only looked away for five minutes"-bit is accurate. The problem with this (and basically ANY disappearance where the parents looked away for "only a second" or "just a few minutes") is that that estimate is entirely self-reported. And peoples perception of time can be VERY distorted. Its entirely possible that the dad THOUGHT it was only 5 minutes, when he was actually having fun chatting for 20. Its also possible that he KNEW it was longer, but didnt want to admit that he left his developementally disabled son unsupervised in a national park bush for 20 minutes. Which doesnt even get into how he searched on his own for a while before getting help, or how the search was apparently a disorganized mess.

It's a blue rose case
So, there's a hiking trail at the back of the town I lived in in Colorado. It's a pretty extensive network of trails, too, all fairly open. The spookiest thing on it is a burnt down cabin covered in graffiti. Now, I'm physically disabled. I really shouldn't be hiking but I really enjoy the great outdoors a little too much to not do it when the opportunity presents itself. I've hiked quite a bit of that trail on two separate occasions, both times with friends from the area. I've hiked plenty of times with them, twice through dense snowpack in just jeans, a hoodie, and a pair of boots. Both times I hiked up that trail in town with them, I did it with a backpack full of beer, water, snacks, and a portable battery for our phones. Not the most prepared, but better than nothing if we had to spend the night on the mountainside. I was the one who carried the backpack despite both my friends being younger and far more physically capable than I am. Maybe it was hazing, it doesn't really matter. On a day where I was off of work and they were both at work, I decided to hike the trail alone. I wasn't *alone* alone. There were plenty of people on the trail with me, I just didn't have a group. I'm making my way up the switchbacks towards the main part of the trail, barely outside of town, and I just feel like I'm getting weaker and weaker. I'm physically slowing down to the point where even some of the older folks are passing me, I'm having trouble breathing, and had to stop to take a break at almost every turn. I've gone less than a quarter mile and am having trouble continuing. Mind you, literally a month prior, I hiked five miles one way with a 20 lb pack through two feet of snow just to check out an abandoned structure out in the woods with my buddies, where we hung out, smoked pot, and swapped stories. I should not be exhausted after a quarter mile on gravel, yet, there I am, sitting on a big rock on the side of the trail, didn't even bring my pack this time, almost wheezing. Once I caught my breath, I just went back down the mountain, back to my car, kicked up my feet, and wasted the day watching YouTube and playing Pokemon.  I still don't know what it was that felt like a weight on my shoulders that day that kept me from going up the trail, but it still bothers me a bit to this day. What would've happened if I had ignored it and pressed onwards? What fate awaited me had I simply kept going? Why did I feel so weak despite having completed far more difficult tasks very recently with minimal effort, at worst a small blister? Come to think of it: why was the trail so populated that day? I'd been on or near it so many times since moving there. The trailhead was a block and a half from where I was staying. I'd never seen it so crowded before. Where was everyone parked? When I say town, I mean almost an insignificant blip on the map. Population ~150, no paved roads, no police, no fire station, no grocery store, no gas station, just a museum open exactly one day a year, a bed and breakfast that no one ever stayed in, a coffee shop open for four hours at a time, four days a week, a bar open Friday and Saturday nights, a post office, a dispensary, and a towing and repair company. Where did all these people come from and why were they all on the trail? I'd never seen any of them before in my entire time there, didn't see any additional cars parked in town, the town is barely on the map, and there are far more popular trails in the surrounding area. I do mean crowded, too. I was passed by ~30 people, and there was a whole train of them going up the side of the mountain. I'd guess that there were 60-80 people just chugging along up that path with very little conversation, mostly just the sound of gravel crunching underfoot. It's so strange, now that I think about it.

Me and my family sware Never to return to the smokey mountains of Tennessee. This comes after our family summer trip of 2022, where we went down the east coast stopping at theme parks. On the way back up to NY, as our family says we made the worst mistake of our lives. We stopped at dollywood then we, as a family, decided to camp in the smokey mountains. I personally felt something was off. At the time I didn't know about the white screamer or the Tennessee mountain man, or any of these legendons. But I got the feeling I was always being watched. We drove up a trail past one of the visitor centers. I'd say after a mile we got to a parking lot next to a historic house. After this we hiked with our gear into the woods for about ten minutes then set up camp. When pitching our tent I saw my dad looking up at one of the mountains. He looked over at me and said we're not welcome here are we. I've never heard this man worried but this was different. He turned and started to take down the tent and said we're going home. The walk back to the car was horrid. My mom always was pointing out that she saw eyes pearing from the trees. And my brother had to hold her because she could barely move due to anxiety. When we did get to the car my mom ran in and got into the back seat with my brother. I tripped and looked into the wood line and saw a horrifying grizzly face. It seemed brutal with cuts and had it's nose caved in. It immediately turned and ran breaking twigs and destorying brush. When I did get in the car my dad got us the fuck out as quickly as possible. When driving out we passed the visitor's center and my dad just frose at the wheel. A figure darted a cross the hood of the car looking at us as he passed. It was the same face, but the body was taller and lanker compared to what I saw in the tree line earlier. My dad nearly crashed on the way out. Eventually we did get to the road and there together we swore never to return to those mountains. My mom sometimes wakes up at night because of this.  Whenever I think about it I feel sick and get the same feeling that I being watched. So I'll say until I die that those mountains are alive. They have their ways and they need to he left alone.

The creek filled up and the heavy rains swept him down and eventually underneath a bolder in a deep area of water.  The pressure of flowing water wedged his body so far underneath the bolder that his body was never found.  His body decomposed there. Respect the mountains, y'all. The mountains around there are weirdly dark. When you get used to the Appalachians, you figure out that different parts have different light and feelings to them. The mountains near Gatlinburg aren't menacing exactly, but it feels like being in the presence of a primordial deity. They aren't particularly interested in you either way, but if you get too bold they might take notice, which you really want to avoid. Other places don't really have that quality. A little further South the mountains feel deeply lonely more than anything. More like there's something sad and solitary there that simultaneously wants to be found and doesn't want to be around anyone. Not threatening at all, but the forlorn feeling can creep up on you.

Are you sure a creature like BigFOOT wouldn't have left footprints lmao. Yeah, it's not Bigfoot, but the thought of falling into pits and getting stuck in one after shattering your ankles sounds horrible.  Also, keep in mind that every human has the characteristics of an ape...because humans ARE apes. Humans are primates, apes and hominids, they just aren't monkeys. So a Bigfoot would be a non-hominid or even hominid but non-human ape with human-like features, and the Appalachian wildman would be a human with characteristics of other apes, such as excessive hairiness (hypertrichosis) which is a type of atavism. Atavism is the activation of ancestral genes of very very distant ancestors, such as excessive hairiness that existed in early humans and still exists in other apes, a tail which is a feature that started off with the earliest vertebrates, the existence of legs in cetaceans or arms and legs in snakes, and so on. It is very much possible that some man who decided to ditch human society due to the stigma society has for anyone who's deemed "unusual", or due to any other personal reason, actually did it. I mean, we have various humans living out in the woods away from civilisation as we speak. Why not?

Another local sasquache-like creature: The Fouk Monster in Fouk Arkansas. I am from arkansas but not the area, so didn't hear much of it growing up. However when I worked in Miller County for the summer (which includes Fouk), I found put everyone has an opinion on the monster. People of all different ages and educational/career backgrounds believe in the monster. Listening to some of them talk was really cool. One middle aged farmer told me he had never seen it, but he had seen signs of it. Like basic structures being built in the woods overnight and weird sounds. A friend of mine from college is from there and told me he believes he saw the Fouk Monster, and he fully believes in it. A coworker of mine at the time was born and raised in Fouk. She is an older woman, and she claims to have seen it more than once. She also claims that it isn't unfriendly, and just wants to be left alone. She told me the documentary on the Fouk Monster is sensationalized. Some of it is true and some of it is known locally to be a complete lie. She also said everyone in the area hates the Crabtree family because of something relating to the monster, but she didn't go into details.   It's a strange town, many of the people are kind of private and wary of outsiders from my experience, but it's a very cool local legend with a strangely high number of believers.

Being an Eastern kentuckian that has spent a lot of time camping and backpacking in the appalachians I can confirm that weird stuff happens out there. Most of it is people of course, but some of it is just very odd.   I've been 10 miles out from any trailhead and run into a dude in street clothes with no gear or equipment, not even a flashlight, as the sun is going down, headed the opposite way on the trail where the next shelter site is 5 miles away.   I've had someone pull open the tarp on the opening to a shelter and shine a light in on us at 2AM, not respond when we accosted them, and then by the time we got up and look out there was nothing. Not even any sounds of someone coming or going.   I've seen a lot of other weird stuff. Most of it explainable just by weird people. But as they mentioned it gets super dark out there and the conditions are harsh. Why someone would be skittering around the mountains at 2am poking into shelters and such i don't know but I can't imagine they have good intent. Just glad there were 3 of us and we stay strapped.   Definitely wouldn't recommend going in there overnight by yourself, and definitely recommend being armed. If I ever did go by myself I'd make my camp off the trail and hidden.

I'm glad you got a chance to see the Great Smokey Mountains. Not only am I from this region, but I've spent about 20 years camping and hiking and exploring the wilderness of this area. I've never seen a cryptid of any kind (that I'm aware of) but I've definitely heard some weird stuff after dark that freaked me out, such as the *knocking* you mentioned. My grandmother was also Cherokee, so I also grew up with stories of hairy wild people in the mountains. I've only been solo hiking ONE TIME in these mountains, and I will never do it again. Nothing unusual happened at all, but the entire time I could not shake this overwhelming sensation that I was in danger. I decided to cut my hike short and return home after less than 2 miles. I've seen plenty of black bears and cougars, but I never really felt like my life was in danger, more like "Oh great, I guess we're doing this today." But that one solo hike made me fear for my life in a way I still don't quite understand. I find that as I grow older I have a lot more love and respect for the place I call home, and the mysterious and almost magical beauty that lives here as well.

Doesn't have to mean Bigfoot and aliens, although absence of evidence is NOT evidence of absence, but things like confusion or hallucinations due to geographic effects esp considering things like recent weather events, granite fields, and nearby sources of water all seem to be abnormally frequent pieces of the puzzle.   As cocky as we are as humans we don't know everything and science/the planet teaches us new things every day. It used to be rediculous that Earth wasn't the center of the universe, that giant squids existed, and that space travel was possible.   100yrs from now if things like these disappearances are explainable bc of newly verifiable things or newly declassified information (bc why is the FBI showing up to missing persons cases from time to time and why the forest service "doesn't" keep a list and makes it so difficult to gain access to) it'll be interesting to know what odd and terrifying but cool and amazing secrets there still are to explore in our world.

As much as I think all of us want to believe these stories of Sasquatch and wild men‚Ä¶ it is much more probable that there is no such thing. We have cell phones and trail cams that should have picked up something by now.  A single hunter in this area can put dozens of trail cams up. Now times that by hundreds of hunters. We got nothing. I don't know how many of you have been alone in a National Park in the middle of nowhere but your mind will come up with bizarre and scary stuff that does not existwhen it gets dark.  No one is immune and it is genuine fear out there. "Strange" sounds happen but in reality it's tiny harmless animals or wind breaking branches. You may swear that sasquatch is fcking with you but actually when you get out of the tent to investigate it's just a badger walking around your camp... The real danger is other humans. National parks are dangerous because wilderness is dangerous. It's much more comforting to think something is killing people than the possibility of one's lack of experience, stupidity, (non cryptid) wild animals or just bad luck being the reason you go missing. If you do go missing the wildlife will make sure almost nothing is left of you except a skeleton but even that will be spread all over and be very difficult to identify or even find.

Okay, this may sound absurd as a wildlife explanation but hear me out. If the kid was silent and nowhere to be found around the trail, what about the chance (though slim) that an eagle (golden and bald seems to be native) came down and attacked. Golden Eagles are very strong and could have crushed his body in some way or just sent him into shock that he didn't cry out. I know it seems silly to think a bird could snatch him, but he was young and may have been just light enough for a bird of prey to briefly lift him away. The family would have very likely not thought to look up, and even if they did it would not be in time for the creature to have gone above brush. It would have potentially cause a lot of noise, so that is a bit of a flaw in this theory, but maybe there was enough of a clearing between trees for the bird to not rustle branches until much higher up? Certain kinds of eagles have been spotted carrying small deer short distances and this could very well be why they saw some shoe prints, alluding to the child getting away for a time (or all together). The helicopters wouldn't be there to see the initial attack and if the bird was able to tear the poor kid into pieces to take home to its nest it's still unlikely they'd see it since it would be very high up and obscured in a nest. I find it odd that the green burges (no idea how to spell this) insisted the shoe size was too big despite not knowing the child and not having the dad's statement on record. Like, couldn't he just tell them what his kids exact shoe size was and go from there? Did they only pack one pair of shoes and didn't have another set to compare it with? Even if they weren't his prints, why would there be one set of child's footprints that far out in the first place? They also did not want people investigating further that side of the creek. Much like they may not have wanted people to know about a cougar attack they could have not wanted people to fear the possibility of a bird of prey. Both bald eagles and golden eagles are native to the region and protected species. If folks heard about this, they very well might want to start killing them or avoid the park. Even if the bird wasn't able to finish killing this defenseless kid, he would be injured and may have then been hunted by something else. Again, since there was a sudden drop in the green burges communication and they deterred further searching in that direction, they very well may have found evidence of animal attack and just didn't want folks to know. I know this might sound like a stretch, but because of that it may be that this scenario may not have even been considered and clues of a bird attack were overlooked.
What they are saying about kid not being able to move through that brush and not being able to climb those inclines reveals they weren't raised as mountain kids. I was a child in 70's raised in the mountains, we ran through the woods like wild things and always barefoot except in winter. My mother kept all the girls hair cut short because she couldn't keep it free of tangles and brambles. That terrain would have been nothing to us and the incline behind our house was steeper than 60 degrees and we regularly climbed it. The undergrowth actually helps with the climbing. Though that kid was likely a city kid, so wouldn't have been able to do these things but to say no child would be able to isn't true.

From a person living in an area that is currently experiencing temperatures of -50F including wind chill, people absolutely need to respect the power of nature. Conditions like that can and absolutely will kill you if you don‚Äôt plan ahead and gear up appropriately.   Most of the missing persons cases in national parks I feel can be chalked up to inexperienced, unprepared, or extremely unlucky (in the sense that several dangerous outside factors stacked up against them) people leaving the trails willfully or accidentally and getting lost. If you aren‚Äôt prepared properly, exposure to extreme heat, sun, wind, wet, and/or cold conditions can bring you to an unceremonious end very quickly. Throw in hostile wildlife and scavengers, and you‚Äôve got a body that probably doesn‚Äôt have a lot of defining characteristics left after even a week.   I don‚Äôt believe these people disappearing has anything to do with the supernatural. Don‚Äôt blame failures in planning and poor crisis decision making on some elusive monster. Take responsibility for yourself and the lives of those around you when you visit the wild places. Plan ahead, do your research, be prepared. Do everything you can to avoid being a statistic.

You'd be surprised how many people will walk by a child in distress who is alone in the woods without doing anything. Whenever I hear about children going missing on busy trails, I always wonder if people just... walked right past them. Not necessarily relevant in this case but I just had vivid flashes of those memories because I was told that my father, my cousin, and my grandfather all took off into the woods and back down the trail when they realized I was missing and hearing Dennis' father did the same, it makes my heart hurt for not just the parents but Dennis. There is something uniquely terrifying about being a young child (I was 9) and wandering the woods alone without knowing where you are. Having visited Gatlinburg TN this past January and stayed right by the Smoky Mountains, it's definitely an understatement to say that they're beautiful yet "dark". A group of friends and I went to a hiking trail in the woods surrounding the Smoky Mountains early in the afternoon. (Probably closer to 10 am) We came to an opening in the trail and we could see the Smoky Mountains a lot clearer than we had before. Though because of how early it was and because it was winter, we couldn't clearly see the tops of the mountains yet. But later on in the day, when we were at this shopping plaza, the morning haze and fog had moved away and we could clearly see the breath taking height and power the mountains had. At night, it was as dark as dark could get. We were staying in this lodge at the edge of the woods. During the day, we could see the mountains, but at night, even though the area by the lodge was well lit, it was as if the mountains tucked themselves away for the night and couldn't be seen until the sun rose into the early morning sky.  I hope you enjoyed my recollection of my trip early this year and you were able to imagine the sights and sounds my friends and I heard and saw during our stay there.

You left out the bearmen. In the 1900s there were like a dozen stories where children were kidnapped by something all witnesses and rescued children described as bears that ran on two legs. For something interesting on cover up reasons i manage a ranch and one day i show up and one of the horses had been attacked by something. It has clear scratch marks and even puncture wounds along with missing parts of skin. Once i alerted the owner, he posted images of the horse on Facebook asking if anyone had any possible explanations with the main conclusion being a mountain lion. Within the hour of the image being posted, a park ranger showed up and basically said "Those massive cat paw prints are actually a mix of horse and deer hooves, the damage is from his hitting the barbwire fence (there is no barb wire fence or any blood/damage to any of the fence) and that missing pieces were from the other horse biting him." The entire reason for covering it up was because they wanted to avoid panic. They even asked the owners to tell some people "Hey, your horse was either hurt by a bad fence or by the other horse".   Even for something that minor, they'll cover it up just to avoid the panic of people storming into the woods with guns

26:45 Tennis shoes are not more likely, as they have become more common over time, but back then were (somewhat) rare, or at least much less common. Tennis shoes/Trainers were primarily worn at school during gymnasium time/phys. ed./sports and normal, leather soled shoes would be worn the rest of the time by most people, especially children who often only had one pair of shoes, especially in this target region. Whether they were "loafers" by modern standards is debatable, they may have just referred to a pair of shoes that either had no laces, or was considered his second-pair of non-good shoes (you had one pair of good shoes for church or school, and another, older, more worn out pair that you wore the rest of the time)

people really underestimate the pure crackhead energy and lack of awareness of a young child. they will walk non stop for fucking ever with the single minded determination of a suicidal meatloaf. we grew up in northern canada, we were told very young to not hide in the woods, stay on the trails at all times, wear bright af colours. we would go on really challenging hikes as small children and just outrun our experienced parents with pure stupid energy. me and my brother were nearly snatched by prowling wolves and what probably saved us was our dad being close and not being too late in the winter. but he only saw them when we got in the car and they came out behind us... my dad is a forestry engineer. he knows the woods. and he didn't see the 4-5 wolves maybe 10m from us. i was a tree planter for a while and it can be really scary how discreet animals are. bears especially, they will pass you by and you will not know. my foreman used to say that 9/10 times a bear met a human the human didn't know it was there. my point is, nature is dangerous, animals will know where you are and might follow your children waiting for an opportunity, or the child will just wander off stupidly far, not being able to be heard by rescuers and die off by exposure, animals or drowning.   also, that wild man description totally sounds like a bear with mange or similar disease. they're really tall when they walk upright and smell like hot garbage. hind legs paws can really look human too. bear skeletons were the basis for giant men myths in antiquity, too. (and yeah i know it's probably not a 'normal' bear, probably a fucked up one with deformities or some kind of sickness. it's plausible. there are quite a lot of legendary beasts who turned out to be wild animals that were hurt or just freaks of nature. not dismissing some kind of ape creature either, but you gotta admin they kinda overlap a bit)

I live in the country just outside of White Bluff, Tn and I have spent quite a bit of time in Craun Hollow, where the legend originates. I can say without a shadow of a doubt that the white screamer exists. The only misconception is that it takes only one form. I have personally witnessed this creature on 3 different occasions, all three having different appearances, but still exhibiting the same glowing red eyes and emitting the same blood curdling screech.  The first one was when I was 11 years old on a hike with my uncle at Montgomery Bell State Park, which is located a couple miles west of the town of White Bluff. It was in the late afternoon and on our way back to the car, we heard some odd rustling and what sounded like a continuous drone or growl just off the trail. The rustling didn‚Äôt sound like walking or something moving through the woods, rather it sounded stationary. We were fairly close to the trail head and I suppose that gave us confidence because we decided to take a look at the origin of the sound. We don‚Äôt have many predators this far west of the Appalachians and the ones we do have don‚Äôt get very large, but when we approached what we thought was the source of the noise, we saw a hunched over ape-like creature that seemed to be digging. Of course we stopped in our tracks and were frozen with either fear or wonder or both. The beast then turned and saw us. That‚Äôs when I saw it‚Äôs eyes burning like two flashlights with red lenses and it let out a horrible scream before sprinting on two legs over the ridge. The moment it moved, my uncle and I bolted in the direction of the trail and didn‚Äôt stop until we got back to the car. The second time i saw it was only fleeting in a car and it was on Craun Hollow road. This time it had taken the shape of an owl but was much larger than any owl I have ever seen. It was perched above the road on a thick tree branch and had the same red eyes I described earlier. When I went back later to the same tree to estimate the size of the thing I saw, I could see gouge marks on the branch it was perched on and by my estimate was about 5 feet tall. The third time I saw it was at a friends house that lived on Craun Hollow and it took the form of a woman dressed in long white robes. We were up late playing video games and just hanging out when we heard screaming outside. When we went outside on the front porch to investigate, we saw it about 30 or 40 yards away at the wood line pacing up and down a fence. We both had lights and when we shined them on the woman, creature, thing it turned toward us and had the same red eyes that i had already seen. Needless to say, we booked it back inside and locked windows and doors. We stayed up until dawn and I left almost immediately after sunrise. After that final sighting, my friend moved out of the house he was staying in and I haven‚Äôt been back that way since. I don‚Äôt know what the sightings were really but they were real enough to spark a deep fear that can only be explained by the words ‚Äúpure evil‚Äù and it‚Äôs partially the reason I was reborn in Christ. It opened my eyes to what the personification of evil can be and Christ is the only refuge from it i have found. It‚Äôs been 8 years since the last sighting and 7 since I found the Lord. I just wanted to put my experiences out there for anyone who might have had a similar one so that they may know there is protection from the evil of this world. It is our savior Jesus Christ. God bless you all.

I have a theory. I think a lot about this story is super weird and I think part of that has to do with how reporting and recording info was done at the time. In addition, as a kid I could make my way through brush and undergrowth that my parents couldn't at all. It's not inconceivable for small children to be able to navigate brush that seems impossible for adults. Anyways, here's where the theory starts. First, it's stated the boy had a slight disability but was still a relatively functional young man. At that time that could be a lot of things, but let's assume it was ADHD or something similar for the theory. I think there may be a chance the boy wandered briefly into the forest as he just got bored waiting to scare the adults and needed to do something.  Then he heard a call to come back, but the way echos in those mountains go, I've heard shouts from one direction that actually came from the exact opposite and I've personally walked off a few hundred yards before realizing my mistake. If he panicked and ran further into the underbrush thinking he was going back he could have made it to eagle creek. I just don't understand why they never crossed that creek after finding the footprints. Their theory about green beret/ FBI involvement leading to no conclusion and they just didn't report anything is likely, but still it's a strange that there's ZERO information on those three days. Unfortunately this doesn't account for why he has never been found, unless he squeezed into a small crag or under a root system to keep warm and passed there in his sleep. Another is that a boy of that size wouldn't be too hard for a mountain Lion to consume in more entirety than when they get adults. And if it pulled him into a den or a thicket, no one would ever find the random bones. This is just my attempt at rationalization though, and I know that it can b pretty easy for all these details to fit an entirely different story.  Edit: i read the ranger report and there were heavy thunderstorms the night Dennis went missing that overloaded drainages and creeks briefly, and they mention the next day was very foggy for most of the day.

Isaac and his mother lived alone in a small house on a hill. Isaac kept to himself - drawing pictures and playing with his toys as his mom watched Christian broadcasts on the television. Life was simple and they were both happy. That was, until the day Isaac's mom heard a voice from above. "Your son has become corrupted by sin. He needs to be saved." "I will do my best to save him, my Lord," Isaac's mother replied, rushing into Isaac's room, removing all that was evil from his life. Again, the voice called to her. "Isaac's soul is still corrupt. He needs to be cut off from all that is evil in this world and confess his sins." "I will follow your instructions, Lord. I have faith in Thee," Isaac's mother replied, as she locked Isaac in his room away from the evils of the world. One last time, Isaac's mom heard the voice of God calling to her. "You've done as I've asked, but I still question your devotion to Me. To prove your faith, I will ask one more thing of you." "Yes, Lord. Anything," Isaac's mother begged. "To prove your love and devotion, I require a sacrifice. Your son, Isaac, will be this sacrifice. Go into his room and end his life, as an offering to Me to prove you love Me above all else." "Yes, Lord," she replied, grabbing a butcher's knife from the kitchen. Isaac, watching through a crack in his door, trembled in fear. Scrambling around his room to find a hiding place, he noticed a trapdoor to the basement, hidden under his rug. Without hesitation, he flung open the hatch, just as his mother burst through his door, and threw himself down into the unknown depths below.

We have many of our own "wild men" stories in Alaska. Besides bigfoot, there are two creatures that come to mind. One is a literal wild man, the other like a skin walker. The first creature comes to fruition when a person is killed by the fault of another, whether that's on accident or purpose. The one who caused the death becomes so overwhelmed with grief and guilt that they run deep into the woods where they see a random flame. The person chases the flame only for the flame to move further and further away and it becomes an endless chase deeper into the woods until the person is driven to insanity and becomes a feral person. They act animalistic and lose touch with society, but they can be rehabilitated if their family catches them and goes through a ritual. The other creature is called Kustaka in Tlingit and Gageets in Haida, and is an otter-man. They can change their shape and mimic voices to fool people, sometimes to their demise. They are stories of them being benevolent, changing humans into new otter-men to save their life when they are on the brink of death, but in most of their stories they are malevolent and will lure people in to either kill them or again change them into otter-men, where they will forever stay an otter-man. Nowadays we don't worry about them so much, mostly avoiding places where they are said to still roam, but you'll still be told to not whistle at night as it can call in the otter-men, and if you hear whistling in the night you better turn tail back home.

Dennis disappeared in 1969 and it wasn't uncommon for law enforcement to keep certain details from the public due to societal values of the time. For example, there's a case from the late 50s in which the body of a young girl (10-12 I think) was found murdered in an abandoned house. She had also been SA'd and her body had been mutilated but the public were only told that the girl had been found dead and foul play wasn't being ruled out. A detective involved in the case was more concerned with preserving the girl's modesty than finding her killer, they prevented the crime photographer from taking photos of her naked body, insisting that the girl be covered up before allowing any pictures to be taken. I'm sure this detective meant well but this interference is, IMHO, a big part of the reason the case remains unsolved to this day.

The Tree People tales your grandfather told you sound like a Native American version of "Don't get into a stranger's truck just because he promised you candy".  It reminds me of the Grimm Brothers fairytales, which were basically compiled German folklore written down for the first time.  Did the creatures inside those stories actually exist? No.  Were they cautionary tales for children disguised in an exciting (and often, especially for children, violent and terrifying) fantastical story while talking about real life threats? Yes. Which lesson is going to stick more onto the mind of a child: A parent telling them to not do something for the 50th time or a grandparent telling them a fairytale about what horrors happened to other children who behaved that way?

Something I always find odd about monster stories: SO MANY of them have glowing [color] eyes. Glowing eyes are a product of human fears of moonlight reflecting in the eyes of predators which is the one easy way to locate them in the dark. Also fear of the devil.   But actual glowing eyes would be such a horrific evolutionary disadvantage for hunting that they would never evolve that way. Having eyes that glow naturally serves only to give away your position and inhibit your own eyes‚Äô ability to perceive external light

I‚Äôm overall skeptical of the paranormal and the woods are damn dangerous. I have seen/heard some missing persons cases that happened in the woods or other areas of nature that are dangerous where what happened was weird as hell but genuinely happened and had nothing supernatural happen. The lesson from the Missing 411, to me, anyway, is that nature and especially difficult terrain and/or weather are incredibly dangerous even when respected and treated with care and deference. Growing up by the ocean instilled a massive respect of the power of nature and how easily it can kill you without blinking. Just animals with rabies can cause enough oddities in the behavior of animals, predators and prey animals alike, that weird shit can happen and be entirely natural if awful.   I think the bit of this video about the family being told that he was found dead and it wasn‚Äôt made public knowledge is the most likely explanation. Animals are damn effective and could most likely take a child without people noticing in the right circumstances.
